3415     /**
3416      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3417      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3418      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3419      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3420      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3421      *
3422      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3423      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3424      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3425      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3426      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3427      * the length of the array.
3428      *
3429      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
3430      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
3431      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3432      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3433      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
3434      */
3435     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3436         if (arrayClass.isInlineClass()) {
3437             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
3438         }
3439         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
3440     }
3441 
3442     /**
3443      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
3444      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
3445      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3446      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3447      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
3448      * <p>
3449      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3450      * the following conditions:
3451      * <ul>
3452      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
3453      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3454      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
3455      *     modes are unsupported.
3456      * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3457      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3458      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3459      *     unsupported.
3460      * </ul>
3461      * <p>
3462      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3463      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3464      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3465      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3466      *
3467      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
3468      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3469      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3470      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3471      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3472      * the length of the array.
3473      *
3474      * @apiNote
3475      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3476      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3477      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3478      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3479      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3480      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3481      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3482      * unexpectedly fail.
3483      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3484      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3485      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3486      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3487      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3488      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3489      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3490      * details).
3491      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3492      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3493      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3494      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3495      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3496      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
3497      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
3498      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
3499      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3500      * @since 9
3501      */
3502     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3503         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
3504     }
3505 
3506     /**
3507      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
3508      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
3509      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
3510      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
3511      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3512      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3513      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
3514      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
3515      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
3516      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
3517      * <p>
3518      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
3519      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
3520      * {@code double}.
3521      * <p>
3522      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
3523      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
3524      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
3525      * of {@code T}.
3526      * <p>
3527      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
3528      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
3529      * with the array and index.
3530      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
3531      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
3532      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
3533      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
3534      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
3535      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
3536      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
3537      * <ul>
3538      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
3539      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
3540      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
3541      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
3542      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
3543      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3544      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3545      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3546      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3547      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3548      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3549      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3550      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3551      * </ul>
3552      * <p>
3553      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
3554      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
3555      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
3556      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
3557      * <pre>{@code
3558      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
3559      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
3560      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
3561      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
3562      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
3563      * }</pre>
3564      * <p>
3565      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
3566      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
3567      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3568      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3569      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
3570      * type {@code T}
3571      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
3572      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
3573      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
3574      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
3575      * array class
3576      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
3577      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
3578      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
3579      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
3580      * @since 9
3581      */
3582     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
3583                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3584         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
3585         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
3586                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
3587     }
3588 
3589     /**
3590      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
3591      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
3592      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
3593      * {@code long[]}.
3594      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
3595      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3596      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3597      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
3598      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
3599      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
3600      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
3601      * <p>
3602      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
3603      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
3604      * {@code double}.
3605      * <p>
3606      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
3607      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
3608      * <p>
3609      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
3610      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
3611      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
3612      * {@code T}.
3613      * <p>
3614      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
3615      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
3616      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
3617      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
3618      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
3619      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
3620      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
3621      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
3622      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
3623      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
3624      * <ul>
3625      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
3626      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
3627      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
3628      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
3629      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
3630      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3631      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3632      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3633      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3634      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3635      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3636      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3637      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3638      * </ul>
3639      * <p>
3640      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
3641      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
3642      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
3643      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
3644      * <pre>{@code
3645      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
3646      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
3647      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
3648      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
3649      * }</pre>
3650      * <p>
3651      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
3652      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
3653      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3654      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3655      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
3656      * type {@code T}
3657      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
3658      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
3659      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
3660      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
3661      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
3662      * array class
3663      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
3664      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
3665      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
3666      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
3667      * @since 9
3668      */
3669     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
3670                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3671         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
3672         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
3673                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
3674     }
3675 
3676 
3677     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
3678 
3679     /**
3680      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
3681      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
3682      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
3683      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
3684      * arguments:
3685      * <ul>
3686      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
3687      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
3688      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
3689      * </ul>
3690      * <p>
3691      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
3692      * the indicated {@code type}.
3693      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
3694      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
3695      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
3696      * <p>
3697      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
3698      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
3699      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
3700      * the final parameter.
3701      * <p>
3702      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
3703      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
3704      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
3705      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
3706      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
3707      * <p>
3708      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3709      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3710 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
3711 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
3712 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
3713 return invoker;
3714      * }</pre></blockquote>
3715      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3716      * @param type the desired target type
3717      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
3718      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
3719      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
3720      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
3721      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
3722      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
3723      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3724      */
3725     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
3726         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
3727             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
3728         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
3729         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
3730     }
3731 
3732     /**
3733      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
3734      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
3735      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
3736      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
3737      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
3738      * <p>
3739      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3740      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
3741      *
3742      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3743      * <em>Discussion:</em>
3744      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
3745      * of unknown types.
3746      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
3747      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
3748      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
3749      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
3750      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
3751      * is unknown.)
3752      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
3753      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
3754      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
3755      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3756      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
3757      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
3758      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
3759      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
3760      * <p>
3761      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3762      * @param type the desired target type
3763      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
3764      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
3765      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3766      */
3767     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
3768         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
3769     }
3770 
3771     /**
3772      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
3773      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
3774      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
3775      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
3776      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
3777      * <p>
3778      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
3779      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
3780      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
3781      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
3782      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
3783      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
3784      * <p>
3785      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3786      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
3787      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3788      * <em>Discussion:</em>
3789      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
3790      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
3791      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
3792      * of the same arity as the general type.
3793      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3794      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
3795      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
3796      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
3797      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
3798      * <p>
3799      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3800      * @param type the desired target type
3801      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
3802      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
3803      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3804      */
3805     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
3806         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
3807     }

3820      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.

3830      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
3831      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
3832      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
3833      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
3834      * <p>
3835      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
3836      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
3837      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
3838      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be

3840      * <p>

3848      *         type.

3859 
3860      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
3861 
3862     /**
3863      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
3864      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
3865      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
3866      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
3867      * which is equal to the desired new type.
3868      * <p>
3869      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
3870      * <p>
3871      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
3872      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
3873      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
3874      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
3875      * <ul>
3876      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
3877      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
3878      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
3879      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
3880      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
3881      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
3882      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
3883      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
3884      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
3885      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
3886      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
3887      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
3888      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
3889      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
3890      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
3891      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
3892      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
3893      *     the low-order bit.
3894      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
3895      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
3896      * </ul>
3897      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
3898      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
3899      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
3900      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
3901      *           necessary return value conversions
3902      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
3903      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
3904      * @see MethodHandle#asType
3905      */
3906     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
3907         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
3908         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
3909         MethodType oldType = target.type();
3910         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
3911         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
3912             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
3913         }
3914         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
3915     }
3916 
3917     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
3918         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
3919             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
3920         }
3921     }
3922 
3923     /**
3924      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
3925      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
3926      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
3927      * which is equal to the desired new type.
3928      * <p>
3929      * The given array controls the reordering.
3930      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
3931      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
3932      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
3933      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
3934      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
3935      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
3936      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
3937      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
3938      * <p>
3939      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
3940      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
3941      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
3942      * or parameters in the target method handle.
3943      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
3944      * type of the original target.
3945      * <p>
3946      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
3947      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
3948      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
3949      * if its index does not appear in the array.
3950      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
3951      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
3952      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
3953      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3954 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
3955 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
3956 ...
3957 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
3958 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
3959 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
3960 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
3961 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
3962 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
3963 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
3964 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
3965 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
3966 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
3967 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
3968 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
3969      * }</pre></blockquote>
3970      * <p>
3971      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
3972      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
3973      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
3974      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
3975      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
3976      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
3977      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
3978      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3979      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
3980      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
3981      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
3982      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
3983      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
3984      */
3985     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
3986         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
3987         MethodType oldType = target.type();
3988         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
3989         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
3990         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
3991         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
3992         LambdaForm form = result.form;
3993         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
3994         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
3995         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
3996         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
3997         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
3998         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
3999             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4000                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4001                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4002                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4003                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4004                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4005                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4006                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4007                 boolean killFirst = false;
4008                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4009                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4010                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4011                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4012                 }
4013                 if (!killFirst) {
4014                     srcPos = dstPos;
4015                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4016                 }
4017                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4018                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4019                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4020                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4021                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4022                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4023                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4024             } else {
4025                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4026                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4027                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4028                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4029                     insPos += 1;
4030                 }
4031                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4032                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4033                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4034                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4035                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4036                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4037                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4038                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4039             }
4040             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4041         }
4042         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4043         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4044         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4045         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4046             return result;
4047         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4048     }
4049 
4050     /**
4051      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4052      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4053      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4054      * Otherwise, return zero.
4055      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4056      */
4057     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4058         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4059         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4060             long mask = 0;
4061             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4062                 int arg = reorder[i];
4063                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4064                     return reorder.length;
4065                 }
4066                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4067                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4068                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4069                 }
4070                 mask |= bit;
4071             }
4072             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4073                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4074                 return 0;
4075             }
4076             // find first zero
4077             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4078             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4079             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4080             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4081                 return 0;
4082             }
4083             return ~zeroPos;
4084         } else {
4085             // same algorithm, different bit set
4086             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4087             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4088                 int arg = reorder[i];
4089                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4090                     return reorder.length;
4091                 }
4092                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4093                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4094                 }
4095                 mask.set(arg);
4096             }
4097             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4098             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4099             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4100                 return 0;
4101             }
4102             return ~zeroPos;
4103         }
4104     }
4105 
4106     private static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4107         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4108             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4109                     oldType, newType);
4110         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4111             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4112             boolean bad = false;
4113             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4114                 int i = reorder[j];
4115                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4116                     bad = true; break;
4117                 }
4118                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4119                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4120                 if (src != dst)
4121                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4122                             oldType, newType);
4123             }
4124             if (!bad)  return true;
4125         }
4126         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4127     }
4128 
4129     /**
4130      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4131      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4132      * <p>
4133      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4134      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4135      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4136      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4137      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4138      * @param value the value to return
4139      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4140      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4141      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4142      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4143      */
4144     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4145         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4146             if (type == void.class)
4147                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4148             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4149             value = w.convert(value, type);
4150             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4151                 return zero(w, type);
4152             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4153         } else {
4154             if (value == null)
4155                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4156             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4157         }
4158     }
4159 
4160     /**
4161      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4162      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4163      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4164      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4165      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4166      */
4167     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4168         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4169         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4170         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4171         if (ident == null) {
4172             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4173         }
4174         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4175             return ident;
4176         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4177         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4178         return makeIdentity(type);
4179     }
4180 
4181     /**
4182      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4183      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4184      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4185      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4186      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4187      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4188      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4189      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4190      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4191      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4192      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4193      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4194      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4195      * @since 9
4196      */
4197     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4198         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4199         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4200             return zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type);
4201         } else if (type.isInlineClass()) {
4202             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
4203         } else {
4204             return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4205         }
4206     }
4207 
4208     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4209         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4210     }
4211 
4212     /**
4213      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4214      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4215      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4216      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4217      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4218      *
4219      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4220      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4221      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4222      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4223      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4224      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4225      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4226      * @since 9
4227      */
4228     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4229         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4230         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4231     }
4232 
4233     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4234     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4235         MethodType mtype = MethodType.methodType(ptype, ptype);
4236         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4237         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4238     }
4239 
4240     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4241         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4242         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4243         if (zero == null) {
4244             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4245         }
4246         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4247             return zero;
4248         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4249         return makeZero(rtype);
4250     }
4251     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4252     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4253         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4254         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4255         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4256     }
4257 
4258     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4259         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4260         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4261         if (prev != null) return prev;
4262         return cache[pos] = value;
4263     }
4264 
4265     /**
4266      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4267      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4268      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4269      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4270      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4271      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4272      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4273      * and calls the original target.
4274      * <p>
4275      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4276      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4277      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4278      * <p>
4279      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4280      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4281      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4282      * <p>
4283      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4284      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4285      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4286      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4287      * <p>
4288      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4289      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4290      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4291      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4292      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4293      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4294      *         before calling the original method handle
4295      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4296      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4297      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4298      *         is the length of the values array.
4299      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4300      *         type.
4301      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4302      */
4303     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4304         int insCount = values.length;
4305         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4306         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4307         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4308         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4309             Object value = values[i];
4310             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4311             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4312                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4313             } else {
4314                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4315                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4316             }
4317         }
4318         return result;
4319     }
4320 
4321     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4322                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4323         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4324         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4325         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4326         switch (w) {
4327         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4328         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4329         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4330         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4331         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4332         }
4333     }
4334 
4335     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4336         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4337         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4338         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4339         if (inargs < 0)
4340             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4341         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4342             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4343         return oldType.ptypes();
4344     }
4345 
4346     /**
4347      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4348      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4349      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4350      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4351      * at some given position.
4352      * <p>
4353      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4354      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4355      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4356      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4357      * they will come after.
4358      * <p>
4359      * <b>Example:</b>
4360      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4361 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4362 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4363 ...
4364 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4365   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4366 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4367 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
4368 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
4369 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
4370 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
4371      * }</pre></blockquote>
4372      * <p>
4373      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4374      * <blockquote><pre>
4375      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
4376      * </pre></blockquote>
4377      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4378      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4379      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4380      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4381      *         before calling the original method handle
4382      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4383      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
4384      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4385      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4386      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
4387      */
4388     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4389         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
4390     }
4391 
4392     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
4393         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
4394     }
4395 
4396     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4397         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
4398         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
4399         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
4400         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
4401         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4402         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
4403         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
4404         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
4405             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4406         }
4407         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4408         return result;
4409     }
4410 
4411     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4412         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
4413         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
4414         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4415         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
4416         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
4417             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
4418                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
4419                     );
4420         return dropped;
4421     }
4422 
4423     /**
4424      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4425      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4426      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4427      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4428      * at some given position.
4429      * <p>
4430      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4431      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4432      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4433      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4434      * they will come after.
4435      * @apiNote
4436      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4437 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4438 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4439 ...
4440 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4441   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4442 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4443 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
4444 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4445 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
4446 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4447 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
4448 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4449 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
4450 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
4451      * }</pre></blockquote>
4452      * <p>
4453      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4454      * <blockquote><pre>
4455      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
4456      * </pre></blockquote>
4457      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4458      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4459      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4460      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4461      *         before calling the original method handle
4462      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4463      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
4464      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4465      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4466      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
4467      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4468      */
4469     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
4470         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
4471     }
4472 
4473     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
4474     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
4475                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
4476         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
4477         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
4478         int match = oldTypes.size();
4479         if (skip != 0) {
4480             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
4481                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
4482             }
4483             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
4484             match -= skip;
4485         }
4486         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
4487         int add = addTypes.size();
4488         if (pos != 0) {
4489             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
4490                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
4491             }
4492             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
4493             add -= pos;
4494             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
4495         }
4496         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
4497         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
4498             if (nullOnFailure) {
4499                 return null;
4500             }
4501             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
4502         }
4503         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
4504         add -= match;
4505         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
4506         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
4507         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
4508         MethodHandle adapter = target;
4509         if (add > 0) {
4510             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
4511         }
4512         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
4513         if (pos > 0) {
4514             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
4515         }
4516         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
4517         return adapter;
4518     }
4519 
4520     /**
4521      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
4522      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
4523      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
4524      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
4525      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
4526      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
4527      * <p>
4528      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
4529      * <p>
4530      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
4531      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
4532      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
4533      * {@code newTypes}.
4534      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
4535      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
4536      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
4537      * sub-list.
4538      * </ul>
4539      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
4540      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
4541      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
4542      *
4543      * @apiNote
4544      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
4545      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
4546      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4547 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4548 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4549 ...
4550 ...
4551 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
4552 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4553 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
4554 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
4555 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
4556     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
4557 else
4558     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
4559 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
4560 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
4561      * }</pre></blockquote>
4562      * @param target the method handle to adapt
4563      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
4564      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
4565      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
4566      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
4567      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4568      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
4569      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4570      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
4571      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
4572      *         {@code pos}.
4573      * @since 9
4574      */
4575     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
4576         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
4577         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
4578         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
4579     }
4580 
4581     /**
4582      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4583      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
4584      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
4585      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
4586      * <p>
4587      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
4588      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
4589      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
4590      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
4591      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
4592      * <p>
4593      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
4594      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
4595      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
4596      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
4597      * <p>
4598      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
4599      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
4600      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
4601      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
4602      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4603      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
4604      * parameter type of the target.
4605      * <p>
4606      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
4607      * (null or not)
4608      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
4609      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4610      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4611 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4612 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4613 ...
4614 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4615   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4616 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4617   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
4618 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4619 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
4620 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
4621 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
4622 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
4623 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
4624 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
4625      * }</pre></blockquote>
4626      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
4627      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
4628      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
4629      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
4630      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
4631      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
4632      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
4633      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
4634      * the resulting adapter.
4635      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4636      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
4637      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
4638      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
4639      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
4640      * }
4641      * }</pre></blockquote>
4642      * <p>
4643      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4644      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4645      *
4646      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
4647      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
4648      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
4649      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
4650      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
4651      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
4652      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
4653      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
4654      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
4655      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4656      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4657      */
4658     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
4659         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
4660         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
4661         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
4662         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
4663         MethodHandle adapter = target;
4664 
4665         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
4666         int index = 0;
4667         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
4668         MethodHandle filter = null;
4669 
4670         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
4671         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
4672         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
4673             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
4674             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
4675 
4676             // flush changes on update
4677             if (filter != newFilter) {
4678                 if (filter != null) {
4679                     if (index > 1) {
4680                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
4681                     } else {
4682                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
4683                     }
4684                 }
4685                 filter = newFilter;
4686                 index = 0;
4687             }
4688 
4689             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
4690             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
4691         }
4692         if (index > 1) {
4693             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
4694         } else if (index == 1) {
4695             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
4696         }
4697         return adapter;
4698     }
4699 
4700     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
4701         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
4702         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4703         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
4704         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
4705 
4706         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
4707         for (int pos : positions) {
4708             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
4709         }
4710         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
4711 
4712         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
4713         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4714     }
4715 
4716     /*non-public*/
4717     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
4718         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
4719         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4720         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4721         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4722         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
4723         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
4724         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
4725         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4726         return result;
4727     }
4728 
4729     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
4730         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4731         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
4732         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
4733             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
4734     }
4735 
4736     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
4737         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4738         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4739         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
4740             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
4741             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4742     }
4743 
4744     /**
4745      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4746      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
4747      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
4748      * filter function.
4749      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
4750      * <p>
4751      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
4752      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
4753      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
4754      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
4755      * not passed to the filter.
4756      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
4757      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
4758      * passed to the adapter.
4759      * <p>
4760      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
4761      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
4762      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4763      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
4764      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
4765      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
4766      * <p>
4767      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
4768      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
4769      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4770      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4771 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4772 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4773 ...
4774 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
4775   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
4776 
4777 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
4778 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
4779 
4780 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
4781 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
4782 
4783 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
4784 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
4785 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
4786              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
4787 
4788 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
4789 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
4790              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
4791 
4792 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
4793 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
4794              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
4795      * }</pre></blockquote>
4796      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
4797      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
4798      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
4799      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
4800      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
4801      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
4802      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
4803      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
4804      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
4805      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
4806      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
4807      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4808      * T target(A...,V,C...);
4809      * V filter(B...);
4810      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
4811      *   V v = filter(b...);
4812      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
4813      * }
4814      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
4815      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
4816      * V filter2();
4817      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
4818      *   V v = filter2();
4819      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
4820      * }
4821      * // and if the filter has a void return:
4822      * T target3(A...,C...);
4823      * void filter3(B...);
4824      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
4825      *   filter3(b...);
4826      *   return target3(a...,c...);
4827      * }
4828      * }</pre></blockquote>
4829      * <p>
4830      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
4831      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
4832      * steps as follows:
4833      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4834      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
4835      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
4836      * }</pre></blockquote>
4837      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
