4838      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
4839      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
4840      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
4841      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
4842      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
4843      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
4844      * <p>
4845      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4846      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4847      *
4848      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
4849      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
4850      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
4851      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
4852      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
4853      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4854      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
4855      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
4856      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
4857      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4858      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4859      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
4860      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
4861      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
4862      */
4863     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
4864         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
4865         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
4866         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4867         LambdaForm lform;
4868         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
4869             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
4870             if (lform != null) {
4871                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4872             }
4873         }
4874         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
4875         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4876     }
4877 
4878     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
4879         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4880         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4881         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
4882         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
4883         if (rtype == void.class) {
4884             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
4885         }
4886         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
4887             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4888         }
4889         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
4890     }
4891 
4892     /**
4893      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
4894      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
4895      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
4896      * <p>
4897      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
4898      * its only argument.
4899      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
4900      * <p>
4901      * The return type of the filter
4902      * replaces the return type of the target
4903      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4904      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
4905      * return type of the target.
4906      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4907      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4908 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4909 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4910 ...
4911 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4912   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4913 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4914   "length", methodType(int.class));
4915 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
4916 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
4917 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
4918      * }</pre></blockquote>
4919      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
4920      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
4921      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
4922      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
4923      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
4924      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4925      * T target(A...);
4926      * V filter(T);
4927      * V adapter(A... a) {
4928      *   T t = target(a...);
4929      *   return filter(t);
4930      * }
4931      * // and if the target has a void return:
4932      * void target2(A...);
4933      * V filter2();
4934      * V adapter2(A... a) {
4935      *   target2(a...);
4936      *   return filter2();
4937      * }
4938      * // and if the filter has a void return:
4939      * T target3(A...);
4940      * void filter3(V);
4941      * void adapter3(A... a) {
4942      *   T t = target3(a...);
4943      *   filter3(t);
4944      * }
4945      * }</pre></blockquote>
4946      * <p>
4947      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4948      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4949      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
4950      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
4951      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
4952      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4953      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
4954      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
4955      */
4956     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
4957         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4958         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4959         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
4960         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4961         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
4962         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
4963         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
4964         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4965         return result;
4966     }
4967 
4968     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
4969         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
4970         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
4971         if (filterValues == 0
4972                 ? (rtype != void.class)
4973                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
4974             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4975     }
4976 
4977     /**
4978      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4979      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
4980      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
4981      * sequence of arguments.
4982      * <p>
4983      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
4984      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
4985      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
4986      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
4987      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
4988      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
4989      * arguments.
4990      * <p>
4991      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
4992      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
4993      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
4994      * of the combiner.
4995      * <p>
4996      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
4997      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
4998      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
4999      * <p>
5000      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5001      * first parameter type is dropped,
5002      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5003      * <p>
5004      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5005      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5006      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5007      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5008      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5009      * target.)
5010      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5011      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5012 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5013 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5014 ...
5015 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5016   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5017     .bindTo(System.out);
5018 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5019   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5020 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5021 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5022 // also prints "boo":
5023 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5024      * }</pre></blockquote>
5025      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5026      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5027      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5028      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5029      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5030      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5031      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5032      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5033      * and arguments.
5034      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5035      * // there are N arguments in A...
5036      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5037      * V combiner(A...);
5038      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5039      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5040      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5041      * }
5042      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5043      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5044      * void combiner2(A...);
5045      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5046      *   combiner2(a...);
5047      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5048      * }
5049      * }</pre></blockquote>
5050      * <p>
5051      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5052      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5053      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5054      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5055      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5056      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5057      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5058      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5059      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5060      *          of the target
5061      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5062      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5063      */
5064     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5065         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5066     }
5067 
5068     /**
5069      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5070      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5071      * before the folded arguments.
5072      * <p>
5073      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5074      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5075      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5076      * 0.
5077      *
5078      * @apiNote Example:
5079      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5080     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5081     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5082     ...
5083     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5084     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5085     .bindTo(System.out);
5086     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5087     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5088     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5089     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5090     // also prints "jum":
5091     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5092      * }</pre></blockquote>
5093      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5094      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5095      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5096      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5097      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5098      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5099      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5100      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5101      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5102      * respectively.
5103      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5104      * // there are N arguments in A...
5105      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5106      * V combiner(A...);
5107      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5108      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5109      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5110      * }
5111      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5112      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5113      * void combiner2(A...);
5114      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5115      *   combiner2(a...);
5116      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5117      * }
5118      * }</pre></blockquote>
5119      * <p>
5120      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5121      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5122      *
5123      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5124      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5125      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5126      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5127      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5128      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5129      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5130      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5131      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5132      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5133      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5134      *
5135      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5136      * @since 9
5137      */
5138     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5139         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5140         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5141         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5142         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5143         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5144         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5145         MethodType newType = targetType;
5146         if (!dropResult) {
5147             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5148         }
5149         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5150         return result;
5151     }
5152 
5153     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5154         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5155         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5156         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5157         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5158         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5159         if (ok) {
5160             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5161                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5162                     ok = false;
5163                     break;
5164                 }
5165             }
5166         }
5167         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5168             ok = false;
5169         if (!ok)
5170             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5171         return rtype;
5172     }
5173 
5174     /**
5175      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5176      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5177      *
5178      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5179      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5180      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5181      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5182      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5183      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5184      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5185      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5186      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5187      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5188      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5189      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5190      */
5191     /*non-public*/
5192     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5193         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5194     }
5195 
5196     /**
5197      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5198      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5199      *
5200      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5201      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5202      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5203      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5204      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5205      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5206      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5207      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5208      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5209      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5210      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5211      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5212      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5213      */
5214     /*non-public*/
5215     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5216         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5217     }
5218 
5219     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5220         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5221         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5222         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5223         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5224 
5225         MethodType newType = targetType;
5226         LambdaForm lform;
5227         if (filter) {
5228             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5229         } else {
5230             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5231             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5232             if (!dropResult) {
5233                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5234             }
5235         }
5236         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5237         return result;
5238     }
5239 
5240     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5241         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5242         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5243             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5244         }
5245         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5246 
5247         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5248             int arg = argPos[i];
5249             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5250                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5251             }
5252             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5253                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5254                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5255                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5256             }
5257         }
5258         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5259             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5260         }
5261         return rtype;
5262     }
5263 
5264     /**
5265      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5266      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5267      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5268      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5269      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5270      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5271      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5272      * <p>
5273      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5274      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5275      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5276      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5277      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5278      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5279      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5280      * boolean test(A...);
5281      * T target(A...,B...);
5282      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5283      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5284      *   if (test(a...))
5285      *     return target(a..., b...);
5286      *   else
5287      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5288      * }
5289      * }</pre></blockquote>
5290      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5291      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5292      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5293      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5294      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5295      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5296      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5297      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5298      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5299      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5300      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5301      */
5302     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5303                                MethodHandle target,
5304                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5305         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5306         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5307         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5308         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5309             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5310         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5311             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5312         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5313         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5314         if (test == null) {
5315             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5316         }
5317         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5318     }
5319 
5320     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5321         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5322     }
5323 
5324     /**
5325      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5326      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5327      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5328      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5329      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5330      * <p>
5331      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5332      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5333      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5334      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5335      * <p>
5336      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5337      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5338      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5339      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5340      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5341      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5342      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5343      * T target(A..., B...);
5344      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5345      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5346      *   try {
5347      *     return target(a..., b...);
5348      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5349      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5350      *   }
5351      * }
5352      * }</pre></blockquote>
5353      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5354      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5355      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5356      * <p>
5357      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5358      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5359      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5360      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5361      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5362      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5363      * @param target method handle to call
5364      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5365      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5366      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5367      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5368      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5369      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5370      *          not match in their return types and their
5371      *          corresponding parameters
5372      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5373      */
5374     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5375                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5376                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5377         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5378         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5379         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5380             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5381         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5382             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5383             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5384         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5385             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5386         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5387         if (handler == null) {
5388             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5389         }
5390         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5391     }
5392 
5393     /**
5394      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5395      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5396      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5397      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5398      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5399      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5400      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5401      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5402      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5403      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5404      */
5405     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5406         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5407             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5408         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5409     }
5410 
5411     /**
5412      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5413      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5414      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5415      * <p>
5416      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5417      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5418      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5419      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5420      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5421      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5422      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5423      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5424      * </ul>
5425      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5426      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5427      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5428      * <p>
5429      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5430      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5431      * <p>
5432      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5433      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5434      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5435      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5436      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5437      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5438      * <p>
5439      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5440      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5441      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5442      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5443      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5444      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5445      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5446      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5447      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5448      * <p>
5449      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5450      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5451      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5452      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5453      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5454      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5455      * <a id="astar"></a>
5456      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5457      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5458      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5459      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5460      * <p>
5461      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5462      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5463      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
5464      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
5465      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
5466      * <p>
5467      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
5468      * <a id="effid"></a>
5469      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
5470      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
5471      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
5472      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
5473      * that longest list.
5474      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
5475      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
5476      * <p>
5477      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
5478      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
5479      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
5480      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
5481      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
5482      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
5483      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
5484      * </ol>
5485      * <p>
5486      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
5487      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
5488      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
5489      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
5490      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
5491      * iteration variable type.
5492      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
5493      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
5494      * </ol>
5495      * <p>
5496      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
5497      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
5498      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
5499      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
5500      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
5501      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
5502      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
5503      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
5504      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
5505      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
5506      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
5507      * the "internal parameter list".
5508      * </ul>
5509      * <p>
5510      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
5511      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
5512      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
5513      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
5514      * type.
5515      * </ol>
5516      * <p>
5517      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
5518      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
5519      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
5520      * </ol>
5521      * <p>
5522      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
5523      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5524      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
5525      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
5526      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
5527      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
5528      * </ol>
5529      * <p>
5530      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
5531      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
5532      * type.
5533      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
5534      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
5535      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
5536      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
5537      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
5538      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
5539      * loop return type.
5540      * </ol>
5541      * <p>
5542      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
5543      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
5544      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
5545      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
5546      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
5547      * pad out the end of the list.
5548      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
5549      * </ol>
5550      * <p>
5551      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
5552      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
5553      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5554      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5555      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
5556      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
5557      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
5558      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
5559      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
5560      * </ol>
5561      * <p>
5562      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
5563      * <ul>
5564      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
5565      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
5566      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
5567      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
5568      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
5569      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
5570      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
5571      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
5572      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
5573      * </ul>
5574      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
5575      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
5576      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
5577      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
5578      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
5579      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
5580      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
5581      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
5582      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
5583      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
5584      * <p>
5585      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
5586      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
5587      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
5588      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
5589      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
5590      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
5591      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
5592      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
5593      * (in argument order).
5594      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
5595      * returns {@code false}.
5596      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
5597      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
5598      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
5599      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
5600      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
5601      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
5602      * except by throwing an exception.
5603      * </ol>
5604      * <p>
5605      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
5606      * <ul>
5607      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
5608      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
5609      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
5610      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
5611      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
5612      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
5613      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
5614      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
5615      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
5616      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
5617      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
5618      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
5619      * </ul>
5620      * <p>
5621      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
5622      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
5623      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
5624      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5625      * V... init...(A...);
5626      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
5627      * V... step...(V..., A...);
5628      * R fini...(V..., A...);
5629      * R loop(A... a) {
5630      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
5631      *   for (;;) {
5632      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
5633      *       v = s(v..., a...);
5634      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
5635      *         return f(v..., a...);
5636      *       }
5637      *     }
5638      *   }
5639      * }
5640      * }</pre></blockquote>
5641      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
5642      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
5643      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
5644      *
5645      * @apiNote Example:
5646      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5647      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5648      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
5649      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
5650      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
5651      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
5652      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
5653      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5654      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5655      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5656      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5657      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5658      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
5659      * }</pre></blockquote>
5660      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
5661      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5662      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5663      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
5664      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
5665      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
5666      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
5667      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5668      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5669      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
5670      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
5671      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5672      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5673      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5674      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
5675      * }</pre></blockquote>
5676      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
5677      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5678      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5679      * static class FacLoop {
5680      *   final int k;
5681      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
5682      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
5683      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
5684      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
5685      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
5686      * }
5687      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
5688      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5689      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5690      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5691      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
5692      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5693      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5694      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5695      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
5696      * }</pre></blockquote>
5697      *
5698      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
5699      *
5700      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
5701      *
5702      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
5703      *
5704      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5705      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5706      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5707      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5708      * @since 9
5709      */
5710     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
5711         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
5712         loopChecks0(clauses);
5713 
5714         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
5715         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
5716         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
5717         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
5718 
5719         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
5720             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
5721             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
5722             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
5723             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
5724         });
5725 
5726         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
5727         final int nclauses = init.size();
5728 
5729         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
5730         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
5731         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5732             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
5733             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
5734             if (in == null && st == null) {
5735                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
5736             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
5737                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
5738                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
5739             } else {
5740                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
5741             }
5742         }
5743         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
5744                 collect(Collectors.toList());
5745 
5746         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
5747         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
5748         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
5749 
5750         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
5751         // Step 1D: check other types.
5752         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
5753         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
5754                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
5755         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
5756         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
5757 
5758         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
5759         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
5760         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
5761         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
5762 
5763         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
5764         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5765             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
5766             if (init.get(i) == null) {
5767                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
5768             }
5769             if (step.get(i) == null) {
5770                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
5771             }
5772             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
5773                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
5774             }
5775             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
5776                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
5777             }
5778         }
5779 
5780         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
5781         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
5782         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
5783         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
5784         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
5785         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
5786 
5787         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5788                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
5789         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5790                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
5791 
5792         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
5793     }
5794 
5795     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
5796         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
5797             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
5798         }
5799         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
5800             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
5801         }
5802         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
5803             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
5804         }
5805     }
5806 
5807     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
5808         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
5809             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
5810                     st.type().returnType());
5811         }
5812     }
5813 
5814     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
5815         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5816         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
5817                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
5818                         map(MethodHandle::type).
5819                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
5820                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
5821                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5822         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
5823     }
5824 
5825     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
5826         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5827         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5828     }
5829 
5830     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
5831         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
5832         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
5833         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
5834     }
5835 
5836     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
5837         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5838                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
5839             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
5840                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
5841         }
5842     }
5843 
5844     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
5845         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5846                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
5847             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
5848                     loopReturnType + ")");
5849         }
5850 
5851         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
5852             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
5853         }
5854         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5855                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
5856             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
5857         }
5858     }
5859 
5860     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
5861         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5862                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
5863             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
5864                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
5865         }
5866     }
5867 
5868     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
5869         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
5870             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
5871             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
5872             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
5873         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
5874     }
5875 
5876     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
5877         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
5878     }
5879 
5880     /**
5881      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5882      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5883      * <p>
5884      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5885      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
5886      * evaluates to {@code true}).
5887      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
5888      * <p>
5889      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
5890      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
5891      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
5892      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
5893      * <p>
5894      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
5895      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
5896      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
5897      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
5898      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
5899      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
5900      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
5901      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
5902      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
5903      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
5904      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
5905      * additional state variable of the loop.
5906      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
5907      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
5908      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
5909      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
5910      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5911      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
5912      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
5913      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
5914      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
5915      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
5916      * </ul>
5917      * <p>
5918      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
5919      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
5920      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
5921      * from the external parameter list.
5922      * </ul>
5923      * <p>
5924      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
5925      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
5926      * passed to the loop.
5927      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5928      * V init(A...);
5929      * boolean pred(V, A...);
5930      * V body(V, A...);
5931      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
5932      *   V v = init(a...);
5933      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
5934      *     v = body(v, a...);
5935      *   }
5936      *   return v;
5937      * }
5938      * }</pre></blockquote>
5939      *
5940      * @apiNote Example:
5941      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5942      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
5943      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
5944      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
5945      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
5946      *   zip.add(a.next());
5947      *   zip.add(b.next());
5948      *   return zip;
5949      * }
5950      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
5951      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
5952      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
5953      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
5954      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
5955      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
5956      * }</pre></blockquote>
5957      *
5958      *
5959      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
5960      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5961      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5962      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
5963      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
5964      *     MethodHandle[]
5965      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
5966      *         varBody   = { init, body };
5967      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5968      * }
5969      * }</pre></blockquote>
5970      *
5971      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
5972      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
5973      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
5974      *             above for other constraints.
5975      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
5976      *             See above for other constraints.
5977      *
5978      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
5979      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
5980      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
5981      *
5982      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
5983      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5984      * @since 9
5985      */
5986     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5987         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
5988         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
5989         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
5990         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
5991         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5992     }
5993 
5994     /**
5995      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5996      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5997      * <p>
5998      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5999      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6000      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6001      * <p>
6002      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6003      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6004      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6005      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6006      * <p>
6007      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6008      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6009      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6010      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6011      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6012      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6013      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6014      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6015      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6016      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6017      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6018      * additional state variable of the loop.
6019      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6020      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6021      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6022      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6023      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6024      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6025      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6026      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6027      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6028      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6029      * </ul>
6030      * <p>
6031      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6032      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6033      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6034      * from the external parameter list.
6035      * </ul>
6036      * <p>
6037      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6038      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6039      * passed to the loop.
6040      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6041      * V init(A...);
6042      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6043      * V body(V, A...);
6044      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6045      *   V v = init(a...);
6046      *   do {
6047      *     v = body(v, a...);
6048      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6049      *   return v;
6050      * }
6051      * }</pre></blockquote>
6052      *
6053      * @apiNote Example:
6054      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6055      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6056      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6057      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6058      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6059      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6060      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6061      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6062      * }</pre></blockquote>
6063      *
6064      *
6065      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6066      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6067      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6068      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6069      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6070      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6071      *     return loop(clause);
6072      * }
6073      * }</pre></blockquote>
6074      *
6075      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6076      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6077      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6078      *             See above for other constraints.
6079      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6080      *             above for other constraints.
6081      *
6082      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6083      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6084      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6085      *
6086      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6087      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6088      * @since 9
6089      */
6090     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6091         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6092         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6093         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6094         return loop(clause);
6095     }
6096 
6097     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
