6098         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6099         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6100         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6101         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6102         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6103         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6104         if (returnType == void.class) {
6105             // OK
6106         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6107             // leading V argument missing => error
6108             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6109             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6110         } else {
6111             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6112         }
6113         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6114         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6115                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6116             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6117         }
6118         if (init != null) {
6119             MethodType initType = init.type();
6120             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6121                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6122                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6123             }
6124         }
6125     }
6126 
6127     /**
6128      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6129      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6130      * <p>
6131      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6132      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6133      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6134      * <p>
6135      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6136      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6137      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6138      * <p>
6139      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6140      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6141      * iteration variable.
6142      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6143      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6144      * <p>
6145      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6146      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6147      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6148      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6149      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6150      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6151      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6152      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6153      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6154      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6155      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6156      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6157      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6158      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6159      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6160      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6161      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6162      * additional state variable of the loop.
6163      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6164      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6165      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6166      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6167      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6168      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6169      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6170      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6171      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6172      * </ul>
6173      * <p>
6174      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6175      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6176      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6177      * from the external parameter list.
6178      * </ul>
6179      * <p>
6180      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6181      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6182      * arguments passed to the loop.
6183      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6184      * int iterations(A...);
6185      * V init(A...);
6186      * V body(V, int, A...);
6187      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6188      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6189      *   V v = init(a...);
6190      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6191      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6192      *   }
6193      *   return v;
6194      * }
6195      * }</pre></blockquote>
6196      *
6197      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6198      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6199      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6200      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6201      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6202      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6203      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6204      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6205      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6206      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6207      * }</pre></blockquote>
6208      *
6209      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6210      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6211      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6212      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6213      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6214      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6215      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6216      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6217      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6218      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6219      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6220      * }</pre></blockquote>
6221      *
6222      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6223      * as loop parameters:
6224      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6225      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6226      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6227      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6228      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6229      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6230      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6231      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6232      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6233      * }</pre></blockquote>
6234      *
6235      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6236      * to enforce a loop type:
6237      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6238      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6239      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6240      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6241      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6242      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6243      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6244      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6245      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6246      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6247      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6248      * }</pre></blockquote>
6249      *
6250      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6251      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6252      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6253      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6254      * }
6255      * }</pre></blockquote>
6256      *
6257      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6258      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6259      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6260      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6261      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6262      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6263      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6264      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6265      *             See above for other constraints.
6266      *
6267      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6268      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6269      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6270      *
6271      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6272      * @since 9
6273      */
6274     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6275         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6276     }
6277 
6278     /**
6279      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6280      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6281      * <p>
6282      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6283      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6284      * values of the loop counter.
6285      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6286      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6287      * <p>
6288      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6289      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6290      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6291      * <p>
6292      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6293      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6294      * iteration variable.
6295      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6296      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6297      * <p>
6298      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6299      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6300      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6301      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6302      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6303      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6304      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6305      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6306      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6307      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6308      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6309      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6310      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6311      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6312      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6313      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6314      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6315      * additional state variable of the loop.
6316      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6317      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6318      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6319      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6320      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6321      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6322      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6323      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6324      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6325      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6326      * to the external parameter list.
6327      * </ul>
6328      * <p>
6329      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6330      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6331      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6332      * from the external parameter list.
6333      * </ul>
6334      * <p>
6335      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6336      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6337      * arguments passed to the loop.
6338      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6339      * int start(A...);
6340      * int end(A...);
6341      * V init(A...);
6342      * V body(V, int, A...);
6343      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6344      *   int e = end(a...);
6345      *   int s = start(a...);
6346      *   V v = init(a...);
6347      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6348      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6349      *   }
6350      *   return v;
6351      * }
6352      * }</pre></blockquote>
6353      *
6354      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6355      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6356      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6357      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6358      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6359      *     // the following semantics:
6360      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6361      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6362      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6363      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6364      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6365      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6366      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6367      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6368      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6369      *     }
6370      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6371      *     MethodHandle[]
6372      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6373      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6374      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6375      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6376      * }
6377      * }</pre></blockquote>
6378      *
6379      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6380      *              See above for other constraints.
6381      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6382      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6383      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6384      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6385      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6386      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6387      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6388      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6389      *             See above for other constraints.
6390      *
6391      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6392      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6393      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6394      *
6395      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6396      * @since 9
6397      */
6398     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6399         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6400         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6401         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6402         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6403         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6404         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6405         MethodHandle retv = null;
6406         if (returnType != void.class) {
6407             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6408             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6409             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6410         }
6411         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6412         MethodHandle[]
6413             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6414             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6415             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6416         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6417     }
6418 
6419     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6420         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6421         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6422         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6423         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6424         if (counterType != int.class) {
6425             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6426             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6427         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6428             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6429             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6430         }
6431         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6432         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6433         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6434         // strip leading V value if present
6435         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6436         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6437             // argument list has no "V" => error
6438             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6439             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6440         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6441             // missing I type => error
6442             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6443             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6444         }
6445         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6446         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6447             // special case; take lists from end handle
6448             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6449             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6450         }
6451         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6452         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6453             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6454         }
6455         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6456             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6457             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6458         }
6459         if (init != null) {
6460             MethodType initType = init.type();
6461             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6462                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6463                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6464             }
6465         }
6466     }
6467 
6468     /**
6469      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
6470      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6471      * <p>
6472      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
6473      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
6474      * <p>
6475      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6476      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6477      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6478      * <p>
6479      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6480      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6481      * iteration variable.
6482      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6483      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6484      * <p>
6485      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6486      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6487      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
6488      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6489      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6490      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
6491      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6492      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6493      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6494      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
6495      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6496      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
6497      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
6498      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6499      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6500      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6501      * additional state variable of the loop.
6502      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6503      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6504      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6505      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6506      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6507      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6508      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6509      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
6510      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
6511      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
6512      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
6513      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6514      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6515      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
6516      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
6517      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
6518      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
6519      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6520      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
6521      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
6522      * </ul>
6523      * <p>
6524      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
6525      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
6526      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
6527      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6528      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
6529      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
6530      * <p>
6531      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6532      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6533      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6534      * from the external parameter list.
6535      * </ul>
6536      * <p>
6537      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6538      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
6539      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
6540      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6541      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
6542      * V init(A...);
6543      * V body(V,T,A...);
6544      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
6545      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
6546      *   V v = init(a...);
6547      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
6548      *     T t = it.next();
6549      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
6550      *   }
6551      *   return v;
6552      * }
6553      * }</pre></blockquote>
6554      *
6555      * @apiNote Example:
6556      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6557      * // get an iterator from a list
6558      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
6559      *   r.add(0, e);
6560      *   return r;
6561      * }
6562      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6563      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
6564      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
6565      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
6566      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
6567      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
6568      * }</pre></blockquote>
6569      *
6570      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
6571      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6572      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6573      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
6574      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6575      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6576      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
6577      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
6578      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
6579      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6580      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6581      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6582      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6583      *     }
6584      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
6585      *     MethodHandle[]
6586      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
6587      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
6588      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6589      * }
6590      * }</pre></blockquote>
6591      *
6592      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
6593      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
6594      *                 See above for other constraints.
6595      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6596      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6597      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6598      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6599      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
6600      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6601      *             See above for other constraints.
6602      *
6603      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
6604      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
6605      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
6606      *
6607      * @since 9
6608      */
6609     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6610         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
6611         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6612         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
6613         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
6614         MethodHandle startIter;
6615         MethodHandle nextVal;
6616         {
6617             MethodType iteratorType;
6618             if (iterator == null) {
6619                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
6620                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
6621                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
6622             } else {
6623                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
6624                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
6625                 startIter = iterator;
6626             }
6627             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6628             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
6629 
6630             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
6631             try {
6632                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
6633                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
6634             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
6635                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
6636             }
6637         }
6638 
6639         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
6640         if (returnType != void.class) {
6641             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6642             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6643             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6644             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6645         }
6646 
6647         MethodHandle[]
6648             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
6649             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
6650         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6651     }
6652 
6653     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6654         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6655         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6656         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6657         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
6658         // strip leading V value if present
6659         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6660         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6661             // argument list has no "V" => error
6662             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6663             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6664         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
6665             // missing T type => error
6666             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
6667             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6668         }
6669         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
6670         Class<?> iterableType = null;
6671         if (iterator != null) {
6672             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
6673             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
6674             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6675                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
6676             }
6677             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
6678             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
6679                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
6680             }
6681             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6682                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
6683                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
6684             }
6685         } else {
6686             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6687                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
6688                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
6689                 // of Iterable
6690                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
6691                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
6692             } else {
6693                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
6694                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
6695                 // assignable to Iterable
6696                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
6697                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
6698                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
6699                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
6700                 }
6701             }
6702         }
6703         if (init != null) {
6704             MethodType initType = init.type();
6705             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6706                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6707                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
6708             }
6709         }
6710         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
6711     }
6712 
6713     /*non-public*/
6714     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
6715         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
6716         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
6717         int[] order = new int[arity];
6718         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
6719         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
6720         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
6721         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
6722         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
6723         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
6724     }
6725 
6726     /**
6727      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
6728      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
6729      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
6730      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
6731      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
6732      * {@code try-finally} handle.
6733      * <p>
6734      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
6735      * The first is the exception thrown during the
6736      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
6737      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
6738      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
6739      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
6740      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
6741      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
6742      * <p>
6743      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
6744      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
6745      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
6746      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
6747      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
6748      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
6749      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
6750      * </ul>
6751      * <p>
6752      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
6753      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
6754      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
6755      * the cleanup.
6756      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6757      * V target(A..., B...);
6758      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
6759      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
6760      *   V result = (zero value for V);
6761      *   Throwable throwable = null;
6762      *   try {
6763      *     result = target(a..., b...);
6764      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
6765      *     throwable = t;
6766      *     throw t;
6767      *   } finally {
6768      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
6769      *   }
6770      *   return result;
6771      * }
6772      * }</pre></blockquote>
6773      * <p>
6774      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
6775      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
6776      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
6777      * <p>
6778      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
6779      * always throws.
6780      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
6781      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
6782      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
6783      * <p>
6784      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
6785      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
6786      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
6787      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
6788      * <p>
6789      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
6790      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
6791      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
6792      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
6793      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
6794      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
6795      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
6796      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
6797      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
6798      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
6799      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
6800      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
6801      *
6802      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
6803      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
6804      *
6805      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
6806      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6807      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
6808      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
6809      *          not match in their return types and their
6810      *          corresponding trailing parameters
6811      *
6812      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
6813      * @since 9
6814      */
6815     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6816         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
6817         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6818 
6819         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
6820 
6821         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
6822         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6823         // target parameter list.
6824         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
6825 
6826         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
6827         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
6828         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
6829 
6830         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
6831         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
6832     }
6833 
6834     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6835         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6836         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
6837             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
6838         }
6839         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
6840         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
6841             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
6842         }
6843         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
6844             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
6845         }
6846         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6847         // target parameter list.
6848         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
6849         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
6850             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
6851                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
6852         }
6853     }
